<Name>Aaron Palmer<//Name><Date>1608853034242< /Date>< pics>

< review>
Haven't visited the south bay in very long so I was interested to see a number of coffee shops that weren't here 5 years ago. Klatch was one of those shops I had never seen before.

As with any new coffee shop, I go for a pour over. They had a nice selection of varying price points, including a geisha (12.95). I opted for the organic single origin they had for 4 bucks. They had an interesting automatic pour over machine that is great since it will ensure that each cup tastes very much the same. The coffee was great. They had great protocols in place with plenty of space inside and curbside available outside. I will def visit again if on the south side.<//review>

< text>
I was already well caffeinated when I saw an unassuming sign with a name I knew, Klatch Coffee and an arrow pointing to behind CVS. Could it be? I thought you had to go to San Dimas to get their coffee.

After parking and wondering, I found their store front. It's facing the corner of the intersection. But almost hidden to the parking lot. Never the less, parking is plentiful!! To my delight, Klatch has expanded to several corners of LA.

Coffee was excellent. Very knowledgeable baristas, as you'd expect from Klatch. I appreciated that they we knowledgeable about Mistobox, the coffee subscription they participate in.

Highly recommended if you are in the area. Way closer than San Dimas.<//text>

<Rate>4</Rate>< review>
"Coffee starts with a conversation"

This is a great addition to the south bay, which lacks a lot of good coffee places! It's located in the corner of PCH and Torrance, right before the entrance of Redondo Beach Pier.

The parking is slightly confusing because you would need to park for CVS and find the walkway around to get access to the coffee shop.

Ordered:
1) latte
2) pour over - Kenya

While I was there, a lot of the people were eating an avocado toast - which looked amazing and made me want to order one the next time I visited the shop.

I loved how informative the baristas were about their coffee and explained the whole process of coffee selection as I was awaiting my coffee.  Great quality coffee is hard to find in the south bay, so Klatch coming into Torrance was quite exciting of its own!</review>

< Text>
My frustrations with PPM are outlined as follows:

Poor customer service: Often times PPM does not post photos of inside of apartments, are not able to provide basic information about apartments such as square footage. There is not a direct line to speak with the person who is processing your application for questions. They will answer text messages, but generally only one text every 2-3 hours, and will only answer 1 question even if you ask 3. Overall very inefficient processing of applications.

False Advertising: Apartments that were listed as "available now" we found out may not be ready for move in for 2-3 months. Although a site may be listed as available, 7/7 properties that we requested already had approvals for other tenants to live there.

Generally not flexible: Unwilling to accommodate minor changes in rental agreements like month-month leases, unwilling to schedule showings on weekends. Move in dates listed set in stone, not open to negotiation.

Conclusion: I tried long and hard to work with this company to get an apartment as the application was fairly expensive ($84 for a couple) but it turned out to be a huge waste of time and money. As a traveling health care professional, I live in many different apartments nationally and appreciate efficient processing of applications and good communication. If any of these things are priorities for selecting your apartment, save yourself some money and a headache - consider other companies before PPM.</Text>

JoAnn SkyWatcher, EFT</Name>
<Rating>5< /Rating>< review>
Arizmendi Bakery has been one of my favorite bakeries to frequent since living in Oakland. It is a cooperative business‚Äîanotherwords, run by the people that work there.

They are very Covid minded. You line up outside the store front. You can look into the storefront window to see what pastries are available. When you get to the head of the line there is a list on the door telling you what pizza and soup is available for the day. The cookies were bundled together for easier buying.

There were 2 people working the front of the store‚Äîone taking the order and money, and the other person getting it and bagging for you.

Their baked goods are fresh and delicious! I have always scarfed down their vegetarien soup and pizza with gusto. Their prices are reasonable.

They look like they are succussful during the pandemic, and I am happy to see that. There are many businesses very close by that haven't been able to make it.< /review>

<username>Jennifer Zilliac< /username>< date>
1578022061326</date>
<rating>5</rating>< Text>
Arizmendi is a democratically run, worker-owned cooperative, which in itself is super cool! All the workers share in the profits. They make good money!

But you may be more interested in knowing that they sell absolutely delicious pizza, bread, pastries, and soups. Everything is as good as it gets. They have a long history of excellence and are not slowing down one bit!

You may also be interested in knowing that, because the workers don't need tips, but people are used to tipping, they keep a "tip jar" by the register and donate the money that comes in to a local non-profit. The non-profit changes monthly. You can always find information about the current beneficiary of the tip jar money by reading the walls.<//Text>

< Review>
I've never been dissapointed coming here!  If you love a good crusty sourdough like me, then you must try Arizmendi! I'll confess it's not the best SD loaf I've had but pretty close to it and only because the Bay Area has too many choices which make the SD competition stiff here. They do, however, make the best heavenly sourdough pizza on earth and offer a delicious daily vegetarian soup that will leave you with a very difficult choice to make.

As for the baked goodies, the almond flour brownie is the best brownie I've ever had and it's gluten free!?! But don't let that keep you from trying it...I couldn't't believe I actually found a GF item I like. Even my kids approve!  Unfortunately, the Lakeshore location is the only one selling it but don't worry any pastry at Arizmendi is great. Croissants are flaky and buttery, cookies are chewy and fresh... You can't go wrong with Arizmendi on any given day.<//Review>

< text>
You gotta love a local co-op (read: worker owned & operated for you non-socialist types) bakery just for the sake of that. But it's successful and it's because it's efficient (even at busy times, the lines moves fast), reliable (whichever of your fav from a wide assortment of pastries, baked goods and breads are almost always available), generally woke (vegan options incl Butcher's Son cheese on vegan pizza) and you can find something for many occasions (breakfast, lunch or bring-something-to-the-party). The coffee is just fine and they got an espresso bar for the fancy types though please skip the "double pump of vanilla syrup BS".<//text>

<Text>I've lived in the bay area for quite some time now and I'm ashamed to say I've never been here.  You will walk in and instantly be overwhelmed with sights and smells.  It smells amazing, it smells like baked goods and coffee.  The 2 best things in life.  I went during the lunch rush hour and that's probably why I was so overwhelmed.

When you walk in, to the left, there's a wall full of amazing baked goods such as cookies, loaves of bread, focaccia bread, scones, muffins, brownies, and so much more.  Any delicious carb you can think of, they have it here.  They even have a bread schedule, on certain days they bake certain breads.  There was sooooo much I wanted to try.  For times sake I grabbed a cookie that had chocolate chips, coconut, oatmeal and some other amazing things.  I also got a slice of the pizza of the day.  They only offer one kind of pizza per day, by the slice or you can buy an entire pie.  When I went they were serving an Indian pizza with Masala sauce and cilantro! Soooooooooo delicious.

<userid>116207656982980496075</userid><username>Bruce Langley< /username><time>1493893957239<//time>< Rating>
2<//Rating>
< Text>
After four years of wanting to support this worker owned cooperative, I've thrown in the towel.
The customer service area is poorly laid out requiring one to stand in up to three different lines for one sitting.
Some bakery items are prepared inconsistently, items with crusts are often baked too hard to enjoy, as one reviewer noted of the baguettes. Soft baked goods like focaccio are usually good though.
Self service coffee urns often run out with no standby urns brewing, meaning long waits for an item that has already been paid for. (the irony of being offered a senior discount and a bicycle helmet wearer's discount on a purchase where the product was not delivered is not lost upon me).
The daily pizza is quite good. They have a new ingredient combination each day, meaning a fresh, hot delicious surprise everytime I come in.  Trouble is that my order gets dropped too often, somewhere between the cashier and the person preparing and serving the slices, one who works six feet away from the other.
The last time I was in (the very last time) I concluded that if I wanted food service like this, I should re-enlist in the Navy.</Text>

<user>107933432659463763637</user><response>None< /response>< Time>
1445411339070<//Time>
< Review>
I've been going to this place since high school--amazing pizzas, delicious pastries. The saddest time was taking a friend here when they were remodeling and closed.

This is the place that has locals coming back time and time again--it's on the list of nearly everyone who've moved to other places and have a bucket list each time they visit.

Favorites: Chocolate Thing, Olive Focaccia, Cheese Rolls, Corn Cherry Scone, Corn Muffins, Pizza--anykind.
Good to know: the baguettes are not your typical french baguette--they are hearty, sourdough with a substantial crust, so be ready.

There's often a line but it'll move fast. And they take credit card so all the easier to carry away a big box of pastries.<//Review>
